<Review>We are not locals, we are from New Jersey and were driving through the area while on a trip to LA and San Diego over the Xmas holidays. We were looking for an Indian restaurant that served decent food without charging an arm and a leg. Mother India far exceeded our expectations.

The buffet was very moderately priced at $9.99 per person. We had two kids, but they didn't charge us for the 5 year old, that was very nice of them.

The food was very good, very authentic north Indian style, cooked as if you are cooking for guests at your home (as opposed to using excessive oil and spices). The best part was the naans - plain and garlic naans, freshly made and served at our table.

If we were locals, we would have definitely made this a regular event. We will be back here, if we are ever in this area.< /Review>< Date>

< text>
I really like this Half and Half location although it does take a bit of a drive to get there. The interior is nicely decorated with lots of cute decorations and furniture. The drinks are the same quality as Monterey Park's Half and Half. I feel like the price is decent for the quality of the drink.

I usually order the iced milk with boba, caramel, and pudding, which is always made the exact same way. The boba is always chewy and sweet and the drinks are always on point.</text>

<user>108010946372978539508</user><name>Cathleen Babbit< /name>< time>
1565722163499< /time>
<rating>4< /rating>< Text>
If you want to sit at the counter, you need to make reservations for it, but my dining partner and I went right when it opened for dinner setting so they were fine with that!  We were the first set and I got all the attention from the chef.

Chef is really passionate about his sake and sashimi collection!  It's clearly displayed at the counter and nigiri is superbly fresh and delightful!  I opted for their Hitachino Japanese beer because I felt like beer more than sake!

The signature wins are his appetizers like his Truffle Chawanmushi!  It was appeasing to the taste buds and smell!  Uni amuse bouche was buttery rich and I couldn't get enough!  I would have preferred for truffle toro to be raw instead of seared. It would have tasted better - textured wise!  Chef took time on telling his background and he came to be in SF.  It was a nice story while dining!

All nigiris were savory and treasured with each mouthful!  I was a bit disappointed that the wagyu truffle nigiri didn't get tossed into my omakase!  I was preoccupied besides requesting for this signature nigiri!  Besides that, omakase for the win here!

Service was lovely!

Lychee sorbet ended the palate - specially flavored and refreshing!< /Text>

<user>103056749735848668078< /user><user_name>Andrew Michaels</user_name>< time>
1507353758693</time>
< Rating>
2< /Rating>
<text>Two word summary: underwhelming and inconsistent. C+ student parading as a an A+ student. If the cost were lower, this would be a solid 3. but at this price, the cost/value/quality was 2 stars

We got the Omakase.

Let's start with the good.
- This is a large quantity of food
- Sake was good
- Some of the bites were delicious--especially some surprise hits, including the papaya dish
- Most of the fish was fresh and high quality; even their uni was delicious
- Chef offered a free revisit of one of the nigiri course (while some omakase restaurants charge an additional a la carte fee)

Now the bad.
- The pacing was a mess. It took 18 minutes before we even started. We were sitting at the bar confused and unsure
- The chef who was in front of us was clearly new, and while I'm down for training, it seemed like he was SO green, he didn't know any of the basics. That's disheartening for a $125 meal
- There was a fly in the fish refridgerator. We notified the chefs, and they just sort of gave up
- In the first course, we had uni on top of crab. The uni was delicious however all three of us in our group had crab shell in the crab. We notified the chefs, and they didn't do anything
- when the first course was dropped, no one said anything to us. they didn't explain what we were eating, just dropped it. We had to ask for help
- as we got into the nigiri course, they started with toro -- two rounds of toro-- starting with that heavy and fatty of a fish seems questionable
- The nigiri pieces were dropped on the same piece of wood, and the wiping of the wood only occurred once every three nigiri, so flavors were blending and not in a good way
- they were heavy-handed on the wasabi, and even after we told them that the wasabi was too strong, and they asked for feedback, they didn't change anything
- the fish cuts were extremely inconsistent from person to person; within our group it seemed like each of us was getting a different cuts of the same fish. When we brought this up, we were essentially told we don't understand how fish works
- some of the fish was cut so poorly that it ended up being so chewy that we couldn't even gnaw through. we left those chunks on the plate, and no one said anything
- On one dish, the sticker of the fruit was still left on the fruit, again we brought this up, and nothing happened (not even a courtesy discount or drink or fish or even acknowledgment )
- The hot dishes came at wildly different temps between our group. One person had chawanmushi that was so hot, she could barely eat it. The other two in our group had cold dishes
- They used truffle in EVERYTHING. It was like a trick they couldn't stop performing. It overpowered the fish, and didn't add to the experience. One of the nigiri servings was literally just a ball of rice sprinkled with flecks of shaved truffle. No one needs that.
- the layout of the sushi bar is problematic. The sushi chef kept asking us to move our plates so he could put the fish on them, and occasionally he gave up and just threw pieces of nigiri on to the plate from afar
- the three chefs were not in sync. Sometimes each chef would tell us exactly the same thing. But, they didn't seem to be working together. It was odd to be so close to that dynamic.

Overall this experience was somewhat bizarre. It felt like an impression of a fine sushi experience, but not the real thing. I think it would have been even worse at a table, so I'm glad that we at least were sitting at the bar.< /text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><resp>None</resp><gmapID>0x808f7e3e373acf1b:0xaf015a2a0f571f4d<//gmapID></record>
</dataset><record>

<text>I have two issues with this clinic. First, I called and asked if there was an avian specialist at this clinic and was told that there was. Although the vets at this clinic will see exotic pets, I do not believe any of them actually specialize in birds. This may have just been an error of the receptionist (who was otherwise amiable and professional). I brought my budgie in for a check up and received antibiotics for a respiratory issue, but when I asked about further tests that could be done if the antibiotics didn‚Äôt work, I was told that doing further tests would be very difficult on smaller bird species. The vet did not seem confident about being able to perform these tests. My budgie is missing half her cere and will likely have chronic health issues relating to this, so I really wanted an actual avian specialist to see her because they have more experience with birds and have dealt with special issues like this. If I had been told that there was not an avian specialist at this clinic I would have taken her to another county. The other clinics who i called in this area were honest about not having an avian specialist at the clinic even if they did see birds.

The second issue was when I got my budgie back. Her first primary feather on her right wing was twisted completely backwards, and her third, brand new primary feather which she just finished growing out on that wing was in the bottom of the cage (along with her older second primary feather). She is molting and only had one new feather on that wing - her other‚Äôs were clipped - so it was easy to identify.  I couldn‚Äôt go into the clinic while the vet was seeing her due to Covid-19 and was given the wrong dial-in number to watch the examination over the zoom conferencing app (which I downloaded just for this vet visit), so I don‚Äôt know how she was handled. I called to ask about this and they suggested that it happened after she left the clinic while she was with me in the car, rather than being accountable for a potential mistake on their part, and I received no apology for how she was returned to me. I was told I could bring her back to the vet, but her wing otherwise seemed okay and I didn‚Äôt want to stress her out further by bringing her back to a vet who may have handled her improperly.

So in conclusion, I am pretty disappointed overall by the lack of information about my budgie‚Äôs health in general, lack of options for follow-up care if the antibiotics don‚Äôt work (which an avian specialist should be able to handle), and lack of care with her handling. I‚Äôm sure this clinic is great with cats and dogs but I  would not suggest taking any birds to this clinic.

On my part, I should have done my research first, but now I am going to find a different vet to bring my budgie to for a follow up evaluation after this course of antibiotics. Currently, the closest registered avian vet is Niklos Webler at Whispering Pines Animal Clinic just east of Chico - found through the Association of Avian Veterinarians at aav.org. I hope this review will be helpful for other bird owners in the area who may be naive like I was.

Since it appears that Arcata Animal Hospital routinely responds to these reviews as well, I hope you will be more careful as a practice about telling people that you will see exotic pets (like birds), but not necessarily having a specialist in evaluating that species - unless I am somehow mistaken. The cost of taking a bird to see an avian specialist is about the same as your fee was (on average $70-$90) and I don‚Äôt think that is right either.< /text><Pictures>None<//Pictures><resp>None< /resp>< gmap_id>

<userid>101491025563625720540</userid><name>Jenelle Bossett< /name><time>1443625223213< /time><rate>3<//rate>< text>
$15 for a basic pedicure....
BUT it did include the spa chairs which was fabulous. I felt so pampered as the chair massaged my aching back. Great with no extra charge!

(If you are getting a media/pedi combo they do not automatically turn on the chair massager so make sure you get them separate worth the extra wait time)

Only negative:
1. HELLA crowded. This place is like a sweatshop of nail care. SOO many stations, always busy, always crowded. Not a long wait time but you will be there with loads of people (great for people watching).

Overall $15 is fair for a basic pedi with spa treatment. If you wanna get the extras like the callous remover and foot massage that would run you extra.

They also do eyebrows pretty well so if your looking for diverse service this place is A-OK!< /text>
